## Text Elements
Exponential family models ^D7JvPMIL

Idea: "If p has a SPECIAL form => some inference learning come for free"  ^UJdakzfs

data ^1hDF9pqW

natural parameters ^aa6zkJ02

T(y) is called sufficient statistic (we'll use T(y) = y).
You can think of T(y) as capturing everything that's relevant to your data.
    Is the same dimension as η. So if you want to have so many parameters you have to have so many sufficient statistics. ^fNJLQC5F

<η, T(y)> ^z7fpmu4S

those have to be vectors of exactly the same dimension ^M7YW7PO1

b(y) is called the base measure - does not depend on η. 
a(η) is called the log partition function - does not depend on y. ^JBs17RnP

y, a, b are scalar functions.
η, T(y) have same dimensions. ^ZwiCvPul

Most distributions follow that form.
Example: ^MgaJH2Az

Bernoulli e.v. Φ an event ^3hAG2jsZ

These examples use concepts of statistics that i don't yet know, so it would be interesting to study it again later ^cWU5W125

Example 2:
  Gaussian with fixed variance σ = 1 ^iCOKWT3K

    MLE w.r.t. to η is CONCAVE ^y7wDtoTx
